interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\n36:  *\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\n41:  *\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \"use strict\" code. The \"use strict\" bit is stored in\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\n48:  *\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\n50:  * different groups of flags:\n51:  *\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n55:  *\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\n57:  * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"did we see a use strict\n58:  * directive\"?\n59:  *\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\n63:  *\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n67:  * can be optimized away.\n68:  *\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n76:  * further into the parse tree. Certain limitations of\\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\\n28:  *\\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\\n30:  *\\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\\n35:  *\\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\\n37:  *\\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\\n49:  *\\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\\n54:  * to \\\"create an arguments object for a function\\\" obviously varies between\\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\\n61:  * further below).\\n62:  *\\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\\n67:  *\\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\\n78:  *     character type.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\\n86:  * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\\n87:  * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\\n88:  * classes.\\n89:  *\\n90:  * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\\n91:  * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\\n92:  * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\\n93:  * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\\n94:  * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\\n95:  * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\\n98:  *\\n99:  * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\\n100:  *\\n101:  * Some functionality depends on character type, yet also is defined in\\n102:  * significantly different form in full and syntax parsing.  For example,\\n103:  * attempting to parse the source text of a module will do so in full parsing\\n104:  * but immediately fail in syntax parsing -- so the former is a mess'o'code\\n105:  * while the latter is effectively |return null();|.  Such functionality is\\n106:  * defined in Parser<SyntaxParseHandler or FullParseHandler, Unit> as\\n107:  * appropriate.\\n108:  *\\n109:  * There's a crucial distinction between GeneralParser and Parser, that\\n110:  * explains why both must exist (despite taking exactly the same template\\n111:  * parameters, and despite GeneralParser and Parser existing in a one-to-one\\n112:  * relationship).  GeneralParser is one unspecialized template class:\\n113:  *\\n114:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit>\\n115:  *   class GeneralParser : ...\\n116:  *   {\\n117:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n118:  *   };\\n119:  *\\n120:  * but Parser is one undefined template class with two separate\\n121:  * specializations:\\n122:  *\\n123:  *   // Declare, but do not define.\\n124:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit> class Parser;\\n125:  *\\n126:  *   // Define a syntax-parsing specialization.\\n127:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n128:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n129:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n130:  *   {\\n131:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n132:  *   };\\n133:  *\\n134:  *   // Define a full-parsing specialization.\\n135:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n136:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\\n137:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\\n138:  *   {\\n139:  *     ...parsing functions...\\n140:  *   };\\n141:  *\\n142:  * This odd distinction is necessary because C++ unfortunately doesn't allow\\n143:  * partial function specialization:\\n144:  *\\n145:  *   // BAD: You can only specialize a template function if you specify *every*\\n146:  *   //      template parameter, i.e. ParseHandler *and* Unit.\\n147:  *   template<typename Unit>\\n148:  *   void\\n149:  *   GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>::foo() {}\\n150:  *\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"36844b0c-67c9-404a-bf4d-4846a45ddc48","uuid":"6c22aac3-0a39-4c48-b38a-a8f6696d313e","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; Certain limitations of\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n28:  *\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\n30:  *\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. It stores\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n41:  *\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\n49:  *\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\n51:  *\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\n54:  * to \"create an arguments object for a function\" obviously varies between\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\n58:  *\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\n61:  * further below).\n62:  *\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\n64:  *\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\n67:  *\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\n78:  *     character type.\n79:  *\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\n82:  *\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive. GeneralParser is one unspecialized template class:\n113:  *\n114:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit>\n115:  *   class GeneralParser : ...\n116:  *   {\n117:  *     ...parsing functions...\n118:  *   };\n119:  *\n120:  * but Parser is one undefined template class with two separate\n121:  * specializations:\n122:  *\n123:  *   // Declare, but do not define.\n124:  *   template<class ParseHandler, typename Unit> class Parser;\n125:  *\n126:  *   // Define a syntax-parsing specialization.\n127:  *   template<typename Unit>\n128:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\n129:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\n130:  *   {\n131:  *     ...parsing functions...\n132:  *   };\n133:  *\n134:  *   // Define a full-parsing specialization.\n135:  *   template<typename Unit>\n136:  *   class Parser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit> final\n137:  *     : public GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>\n138:  *   {\n139:  *     ...parsing functions...\n140:  *   };\n141:  *\n142:  * This odd distinction is necessary because C++ unfortunately doesn't allow\n143:  * partial function specialization:\n144:  *\n145:  *   // BAD: You can only specialize a template function if you specify *every*\n146:  *   //      template parameter, i.e. ParseHandler *and* Unit.\n147:  *   template<typename Unit>\n148:  *   void\n149:  *   GeneralParser<SyntaxParseHandler, Unit>::foo() {}\n150:  *\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-150"}}}

Bytecode has many consumers, not just the interpreter: JITs,\\n46:  * analyses, the debugger. That's why the rules below apply even to code that\\n47:  * can't be reached in ordinary execution (such as code after an infinite loop\\n48:  * or inside an `if (false)` block).\\n49:  *\\n50:  * The `code()` of a script must be a packed (not aligned) sequence of valid\\n51:  * instructions from start to end. Each instruction has a single byte opcode\\n52:  * followed by a number of operand bytes based on the opcode.\\n53:  *\\n54:  * ## Jump instructions\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Operands named `offset`, `forwardOffset`, or `defaultOffset` are jump\\n57:  * offsets, the distance in bytes from the start of the current instruction to\\n58:  * the start of another instruction in the same script. Operands named\\n59:  * `forwardOffset` or `defaultOffset` must be positive.\\n60:  *\\n61:  * Forward jumps must jump to a `JSOp::JumpTarget` instruction.  Backward jumps,\\n62:  * indicated by negative offsets, must jump to a `JSOp::LoopHead` instruction.\\n63:  * Jump offsets can't be zero.\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Needless to say, scripts must not contain overlapping instruction sequences\\n66:  * (in the sense of <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overlapping_gene>).\\n67:  *\\n68:  * A script's `trynotes` and `scopeNotes` impose further constraints. Each try\\n69:  * note and each scope note marks a region of the bytecode where some invariant\\n70:  * holds, or some cleanup behavior is needed--that there's a for-in iterator in\\n71:  * a particular stack slot, for instance, which must be closed on error. All\\n72:  * paths into the span must establish that invariant. In practice, this means\\n73:  * other code never jumps into the span: the only way in is to execute the\\n74:  * bytecode instruction that sets up the invariant (in our example,\\n75:  * `JSOp::Iter`).\\n76:  *\\n77:  * If a script's `trynotes` (see \\\"Try Notes\\\" in JSScript.h) contain a\\n78:  * `JSTRY_CATCH` or `JSTRY_FINALLY` span, there must be a `JSOp::Try`\\n79:  * instruction immediately before the span and a `JSOp::JumpTarget immediately\\n80:  * after it. Instructions must not jump to this `JSOp::JumpTarget`. (The VM puts\\n81:  * us there on exception.) Furthermore, the instruction sequence immediately\\n82:  * following a `JSTRY_CATCH` span must read `JumpTarget; Exception` or, in\\n83:  * non-function scripts, `JumpTarget; Undefined; SetRval; Exception`. (These\\n84:  * instructions run with an exception pending; other instructions aren't\\n85:  * designed to handle that.)\\n86:  *\\n87:  * Unreachable instructions are allowed, but they have to follow all the rules.\\n88:  *\\n89:  * Control must not reach the end of a script. (Currently, the last instruction\\n90:  * is always JSOp::RetRval.)\\n91:  *\\n92:  * ## Other operands\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Operands named `nameIndex` or `atomIndex` (which appear on instructions that\\n95:  * have `JOF_ATOM` in the `format` field) must be valid indexes into\\n96:  * `script->atoms()`.\\n97:  *\\n98:  * Operands named `argc` (`JOF_ARGC`) are argument counts for call\\n99:  * instructions. `argc` must be small enough that the instruction's nuses is <=\\n100:  * the current stack depth (see \\\"Stack depth\\\" below).\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/vm/Opcodes.h%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"36844b0c-67c9-404a-bf4d-4846a45ddc48","uuid":"5dd46a96-15de-419a-af34-5501c88eaedd","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sw=2 et tw=0 ft=c:\\n3:  *\\n4:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n5:  * License, v. 2.0.
